<p><b>Taipei</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/ secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/aɪ/ long 'i' in 'tide'">aɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/eɪ/ long 'a' in 'base'">eɪ</span></span>/</a></span></span>), officially known as <b>Taipei City</b>, is the capital city and a <a href="/wiki/Special_municipality_(Taiwan)" title="Special municipality (Taiwan)">special municipality</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Republic of China</a> (commonly known as Taiwan) serving as the seat of the central government. Sitting at the northern tip of the state, Taipei City is an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enclave" title="Enclave">enclave</a> of the municipality of <a href="/wiki/New_Taipei_City" title="New Taipei City">New Taipei City</a>. It is about 25 km (16 mi) southwest of the northern port city <a href="/wiki/Keelung" title="Keelung">Keelung</a>. Most of the city is located on the <a href="/wiki/Taipei_Basin" title="Taipei Basin">Taipei Basin</a>, an ancient lakebed bounded by the two relatively narrow valleys of the <a href="/wiki/Keelung_River" title="Keelung River">Keelung</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xindian_River" title="Xindian River">Xindian</a> rivers, which join to form the <a href="/wiki/Tamsui_River" title="Tamsui River">Tamsui River</a> along the city's western border.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcggeo_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-tcggeo-5">[5]</a></sup> Since 1949, Taipei has been the <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">capital</a> of the ROC after losing the <a href="/wiki/Mainland_China" title="Mainland China">mainland</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_China" title="Communist Party of China">Communists</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">Chinese Civil War</a>.</p>
<p>The city proper is home to an estimated population of 2,704,810 in 2015,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-population_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-population-6">[6]</a></sup> forming the core part of the <a href="/wiki/Taipei%E2%80%93Keelung_metropolitan_area" title="Taipei–Keelung metropolitan area">Taipei–Keelung metropolitan area</a> which includes the nearby cities of New Taipei and Keelung with a population of 7,047,559,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-population_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-population-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> the 40th most-populous urban area in the world—roughly one-third of Taiwanese citizens live in the metro district. The name "Taipei" can refer either to the whole metropolitan area or the city proper.</p>
<p>Taipei is the political, economic, educational, and cultural center of Taiwan, and one of the major hubs of the Chinese-speaking world. Considered to be a <a href="/wiki/Global_city" title="Global city">global city</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> Taipei is part of a major high-tech industrial area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Taiwan" title="Rail transport in Taiwan">Railways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_High_Speed_Rail" title="Taiwan High Speed Rail">high-speed rail</a>, <a href="/wiki/Highway_system_in_Taiwan" title="Highway system in Taiwan">highways</a>, airports, and bus lines connect Taipei with all parts of the island. The city is served by two airports – <a href="/wiki/Taipei_Songshan_Airport" title="Taipei Songshan Airport">Taipei Songshan</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taiwan_Taoyuan_International_Airport" title="Taiwan Taoyuan International Airport">Taiwan Taoyuan</a>. Taipei is home to various world-famous architectural or cultural landmarks which include <a href="/wiki/Taipei_101" title="Taipei 101">Taipei 101</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek_Memorial_Hall" title="Chiang Kai-shek Memorial Hall">Chiang Kai-shek Memorial Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dalongdong_Baoan_Temple" title="Dalongdong Baoan Temple">Dalongdong Baoan Temple</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hsing_Tian_Kong" title="Hsing Tian Kong">Hsing Tian Kong</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mengjia_Longshan_Temple" title="Mengjia Longshan Temple">Mengjia Longshan Temple</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Palace_Museum" title="National Palace Museum">National Palace Museum</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Presidential_Office_Building,_Taipei" title="Presidential Office Building, Taipei">Presidential Office Building</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taipei_Guest_House" title="Taipei Guest House">Taipei Guest House</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ximending" title="Ximending">Ximending</a>, and several <a href="/wiki/Night_markets_in_Taiwan" title="Night markets in Taiwan">night markets</a> dispersing over the city. Its natural features such as <a href="/wiki/Maokong" title="Maokong">Maokong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yangmingshan" title="Yangmingshan">Yangmingshan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Taiwanese_hot_springs" title="Taiwanese hot springs">hot springs</a> are also well known to international visitors.</p>
<p>As the capital city, "Taipei" is sometimes used as a <a href="/wiki/Synecdoche" title="Synecdoche">synecdoche</a> for Taiwan. Due to the ongoing controversy over the <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_Taiwan" title="Political status of Taiwan">political status of Taiwan</a>, the name <i><a href="/wiki/Chinese_Taipei" title="Chinese Taipei">Chinese Taipei</a></i> is designated for official use when Taiwanese governmental representatives or national teams participate in some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_organizations" title="International organizations">international organizations</a> or international sporting events (which may require <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">UN statehood</a>) in order to avoid extensive political controversy by using other names.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Taipei" title="History of Taipei">History of Taipei</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Old_street,_Taipei.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Old_street%2C_Taipei.jpg/220px-Old_street%2C_Taipei.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Old_street%2C_Taipei.jpg/330px-Old_street%2C_Taipei.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Old_street%2C_Taipei.jpg/440px-Old_street%2C_Taipei.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Old_street,_Taipei.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Old street in Taipei in 2013</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Prior to the significant influx of Han Chinese immigrants, the region of Taipei Basin was mainly inhabited by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ketagalan" title="Ketagalan">Ketagalan</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taiwanese_plains_aborigines" title="Taiwanese plains aborigines">plains aborigines</a>. The number of Han immigrants gradually increased in the early 18th century under <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_under_Qing_rule" title="Taiwan under Qing rule">Qing Dynasty rule</a> after the government began permitting development in the area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> In 1875, the northern part of the island was incorporated into the new <a href="/wiki/Taipeh_Prefecture" title="Taipeh Prefecture">Taipeh Prefecture</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty" title="Qing dynasty">Qing dynasty</a> of China made Taipei the temporary capital of <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_Province#Qing_Dynasty" title="Taiwan Province">Fujian-Taiwan Province</a> in 1886 when Taiwan was separated from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fujian_Province" title="Fujian Province">Fujian Province</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Taipeh was formally made the provincial capital in 1894.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> acquired Taiwan in 1895 under the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Shimonoseki" title="Treaty of Shimonoseki">Treaty of Shimonoseki</a> after the <a href="/wiki/First_Sino-Japanese_War" title="First Sino-Japanese War">First Sino-Japanese War</a>. Taiwan became <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_under_Japanese_rule" title="Taiwan under Japanese rule">a colony of Imperial Japan</a> with <i>Taihoku</i> (formerly Taipeh) as its capital, in which the city was administered under <a href="/wiki/Taihoku_Prefecture" title="Taihoku Prefecture">Taihoku Prefecture</a>. Taiwan's Japanese rulers embarked on an extensive program of advanced <a href="/wiki/Urban_planning" title="Urban planning">urban planning</a> that featured extensive railroad links. A number of Taipei landmarks and cultural institutions date from this period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-marsh1_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-marsh1-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Surrender_of_Japan" title="Surrender of Japan">Japanese surrender</a> of 1945, control of Taiwan was handed to the Republic of China (ROC) (see <a href="/wiki/Retrocession_Day" title="Retrocession Day">Retrocession Day</a>). After losing <a href="/wiki/Mainland_China" title="Mainland China">mainland China</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_China" title="Communist Party of China">Chinese Communist Party</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">Chinese Civil War</a>, the ruling <a href="/wiki/Kuomintang" title="Kuomintang">Kuomintang</a> (KMT) relocated the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_Republic_of_China" title="Government of the Republic of China">ROC government</a> to Taiwan and declared Taipei the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Provisional_capital" title="Provisional capital">provisional capital</a> of the ROC in December 1949.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ng_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-ng-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbctimeline-retreat_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbctimeline-retreat-15">[15]</a></sup> In 1990 Taipei provided the backdrop for the <a href="/wiki/Wild_Lily_student_movement" title="Wild Lily student movement">Wild Lily student rallies</a> that moved Taiwanese society from one-party rule to multi-party <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a>. The city is today home to Taiwan's democratically elected national government.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_settlements">First settlements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: First settlements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The region known as the <a href="/wiki/Taipei_Basin" title="Taipei Basin">Taipei Basin</a> was home to <a href="/wiki/Ketagalan_people" title="Ketagalan people">Ketagalan</a> tribes before the eighteenth century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Han Chinese</a> mainly from <a href="/wiki/Fujian" title="Fujian">Fujian</a> Province of Qing dynasty China began to settle in the Taipei Basin in 1709.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kelly_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-kelly-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcghistory_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-tcghistory-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the late 19th century, the Taipei area, where the major Han Chinese settlements in northern Taiwan and one of the designated overseas trade ports, <a href="/wiki/Tamsui_District" title="Tamsui District">Tamsui</a>, were located, gained economic importance due to the booming overseas trade, especially that of <a href="/wiki/Tea" title="Tea">tea</a> export. In 1875, the northern part of Taiwan was separated from <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_Prefecture" title="Taiwan Prefecture">Taiwan Prefecture</a> and incorporated into the new <a href="/wiki/Taipeh_Prefecture" title="Taipeh Prefecture">Taipeh Prefecture</a> as a new administrative entity of the Qing dynasty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-marsh1_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-marsh1-13">[13]</a></sup> Having been established adjoining the flourishing townships of <a href="/wiki/Wanhua_District" title="Wanhua District">Bangka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dalongdong" title="Dalongdong">Dalongdong</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Twatutia" title="Twatutia">Twatutia</a>, the new prefectural capital was known as <i>Chengnei</i> (<a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh">城內</span>; <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">pinyin</a>: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">chéngnèi</span></i>; <a href="/wiki/Pe%CC%8Dh-%C5%8De-j%C4%AB" title="Pe̍h-ōe-jī">Pe̍h-ōe-jī</a>: <i><span lang="nan">siâⁿ-lāi</span></i>), "the inner city", and government buildings were erected there. From 1875 (still Qing era) until the beginning of Japanese rule in 1895, Taipei was part of Tamsui County of Taipeh Prefecture and the prefectural capital.</p>
<p>In 1885, work commenced to create an independent Taiwan Province, and Taipei City was temporarily made the provincial capital. Taipei officially became the capital of Taiwan in 1894.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> All that remains from the Qing era is the north gate. The west gate and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taipei_City_Walls" title="Taipei City Walls">city walls</a> were demolished by the Japanese while the south gate, little south gate, and east gate were extensively modified by the <a href="/wiki/Kuomintang" title="Kuomintang">Kuomintang</a> (KMT) and have lost much of their original character.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Empire_of_Japan">Empire of Japan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Empire of Japan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%E5%A4%A7%E5%B3%B6%E4%B9%85%E6%BB%BF%E6%AC%A1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="261" data-file-width="480" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/%E5%A4%A7%E5%B3%B6%E4%B9%85%E6%BB%BF%E6%AC%A1.jpg/220px-%E5%A4%A7%E5%B3%B6%E4%B9%85%E6%BB%BF%E6%AC%A1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/%E5%A4%A7%E5%B3%B6%E4%B9%85%E6%BB%BF%E6%AC%A1.jpg/330px-%E5%A4%A7%E5%B3%B6%E4%B9%85%E6%BB%BF%E6%AC%A1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/%E5%A4%A7%E5%B3%B6%E4%B9%85%E6%BB%BF%E6%AC%A1.jpg/440px-%E5%A4%A7%E5%B3%B6%E4%B9%85%E6%BB%BF%E6%AC%A1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%E5%A4%A7%E5%B3%B6%E4%B9%85%E6%BB%BF%E6%AC%A1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Taihoku_Prefecture" title="Taihoku Prefecture">Taihoku Prefecture</a> government building in the 1910s (now the <a href="/wiki/Control_Yuan" title="Control Yuan">Control Yuan</a>)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As settlement for losing the <a href="/wiki/First_Sino-Japanese_War" title="First Sino-Japanese War">First Sino-Japanese War</a>, China ceded the island of Taiwan to the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Empire of Japan</a> in 1895 as part of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Shimonoseki" title="Treaty of Shimonoseki">Treaty of Shimonoseki</a>. After the Japanese take-over, Taipei, called <b>Taihoku</b> in Japanese, was retained as the capital and emerged as the political center of the Japanese Colonial Government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-marsh1_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-marsh1-13">[13]</a></sup> During that time the city acquired the characteristics of an administrative center, including many new public buildings and <a href="/wiki/Qidong_Street_Japanese_Houses" title="Qidong Street Japanese Houses">housing for civil servants</a>. Much of the architecture of Taipei dates from the period of <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_under_Japanese_rule" title="Taiwan under Japanese rule">Japanese rule</a>, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Presidential_Office_Building,_Taipei" title="Presidential Office Building, Taipei">Presidential Building</a> which was the Office of the <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_Taiwan" title="Governor-General of Taiwan">Governor-General of Taiwan</a>.</p>
<p>During Japanese rule, Taihoku was incorporated in 1920 as part of <a href="/wiki/Taihoku_Prefecture" title="Taihoku Prefecture">Taihoku Prefecture</a>. It included <a href="/wiki/Wanhua_District" title="Wanhua District">Bangka</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Twatutia" title="Twatutia">Twatutia</a>, and <i>Jōnai</i> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">城內</span><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span> among other small settlements. The eastern village of <i>Matsuyama</i> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">松山庄</span>, modern-day <a href="/wiki/Songshan_District,_Taipei" title="Songshan District, Taipei">Songshan District, Taipei</a>)</span> was annexed into Taihoku City in 1938. Upon the Japanese defeat in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_War" title="Pacific War">Pacific War</a> and its consequent surrender in August 1945, the <a href="/wiki/Kuomintang" title="Kuomintang">Kuomintang</a> (Chinese Nationalist Party) assumed control of Taiwan. Subsequently, a temporary Office of the Taiwan Province Administrative Governor was established in Taipei City.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh199685_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh199685-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Republic_of_China">Republic of China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Republic of China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:U.S._President_Eisenhower_visited_TAIWAN_%E7%BE%8E%E5%9C%8B%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1%E8%89%BE%E6%A3%AE%E8%B1%AA%E6%96%BC1960%E5%B9%B46%E6%9C%88%E8%A8%AA%E5%95%8F%E8%87%BA%E7%81%A3%E5%8F%B0%E5%8C%97%E6%99%82%E8%88%87%E8%94%A3%E4%B8%AD%E6%AD%A3%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1-2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="689" data-file-width="1102" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/U.S._President_Eisenhower_visited_TAIWAN_%E7%BE%8E%E5%9C%8B%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1%E8%89%BE%E6%A3%AE%E8%B1%AA%E6%96%BC1960%E5%B9%B46%E6%9C%88%E8%A8%AA%E5%95%8F%E8%87%BA%E7%81%A3%E5%8F%B0%E5%8C%97%E6%99%82%E8%88%87%E8%94%A3%E4%B8%AD%E6%AD%A3%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1-2.jpg/220px-U.S._President_Eisenhower_visited_TAIWAN_%E7%BE%8E%E5%9C%8B%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1%E8%89%BE%E6%A3%AE%E8%B1%AA%E6%96%BC1960%E5%B9%B46%E6%9C%88%E8%A8%AA%E5%95%8F%E8%87%BA%E7%81%A3%E5%8F%B0%E5%8C%97%E6%99%82%E8%88%87%E8%94%A3%E4%B8%AD%E6%AD%A3%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1-2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/U.S._President_Eisenhower_visited_TAIWAN_%E7%BE%8E%E5%9C%8B%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1%E8%89%BE%E6%A3%AE%E8%B1%AA%E6%96%BC1960%E5%B9%B46%E6%9C%88%E8%A8%AA%E5%95%8F%E8%87%BA%E7%81%A3%E5%8F%B0%E5%8C%97%E6%99%82%E8%88%87%E8%94%A3%E4%B8%AD%E6%AD%A3%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1-2.jpg/330px-U.S._President_Eisenhower_visited_TAIWAN_%E7%BE%8E%E5%9C%8B%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1%E8%89%BE%E6%A3%AE%E8%B1%AA%E6%96%BC1960%E5%B9%B46%E6%9C%88%E8%A8%AA%E5%95%8F%E8%87%BA%E7%81%A3%E5%8F%B0%E5%8C%97%E6%99%82%E8%88%87%E8%94%A3%E4%B8%AD%E6%AD%A3%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/U.S._President_Eisenhower_visited_TAIWAN_%E7%BE%8E%E5%9C%8B%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1%E8%89%BE%E6%A3%AE%E8%B1%AA%E6%96%BC1960%E5%B9%B46%E6%9C%88%E8%A8%AA%E5%95%8F%E8%87%BA%E7%81%A3%E5%8F%B0%E5%8C%97%E6%99%82%E8%88%87%E8%94%A3%E4%B8%AD%E6%AD%A3%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1-2.jpg/440px-U.S._President_Eisenhower_visited_TAIWAN_%E7%BE%8E%E5%9C%8B%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1%E8%89%BE%E6%A3%AE%E8%B1%AA%E6%96%BC1960%E5%B9%B46%E6%9C%88%E8%A8%AA%E5%95%8F%E8%87%BA%E7%81%A3%E5%8F%B0%E5%8C%97%E6%99%82%E8%88%87%E8%94%A3%E4%B8%AD%E6%AD%A3%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1-2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:U.S._President_Eisenhower_visited_TAIWAN_%E7%BE%8E%E5%9C%8B%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1%E8%89%BE%E6%A3%AE%E8%B1%AA%E6%96%BC1960%E5%B9%B46%E6%9C%88%E8%A8%AA%E5%95%8F%E8%87%BA%E7%81%A3%E5%8F%B0%E5%8C%97%E6%99%82%E8%88%87%E8%94%A3%E4%B8%AD%E6%AD%A3%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1-2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
With President <a href="/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek" title="Chiang Kai-shek">Chiang Kai-shek</a>, U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight D. Eisenhower</a> waved to a crowd during his visit to Taipei in June 1960.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1947 the KMT government under <a href="/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek" title="Chiang Kai-shek">Chiang Kai-shek</a> declared island-wide <a href="/wiki/Martial_law_in_Taiwan" title="Martial law in Taiwan">martial law in Taiwan</a> as a result of the <a href="/wiki/February_28_Incident" title="February 28 Incident">February 28 Incident</a>, which began with incidents in Taipei but led to an island-wide crackdown on the local population by forces loyal to Chiang. Two years later, on December 7, 1949, Chiang and the Kuomintang were forced to flee mainland China by the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_China" title="Communist Party of China">Communists</a> near the end of the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">Chinese Civil War</a>. The refugees declared Taipei to be the provisional capital of a continuing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912%E2%80%931949)" title="Republic of China (1912–1949)">Republic of China</a>, with the official capital at <a href="/wiki/Nanjing" title="Nanjing">Nanjing</a> (Nanking) even though that city was under Communist control.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ng_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-ng-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbctimeline-retreat_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbctimeline-retreat-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Taipei <a href="/wiki/Military_dependents%27_village" title="Military dependents' village">expanded greatly</a> in the decades after 1949, and as approved on December 30, 1966 by the <a href="/wiki/Executive_Yuan" title="Executive Yuan">Executive Yuan</a>, Taipei was declared a special <a href="/wiki/Direct-controlled_municipality" title="Direct-controlled municipality">centrally administered municipality</a> on July 1, 1967 and given the administrative status of a province.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcghistory_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-tcghistory-18">[18]</a></sup> In the following year, Taipei City expanded again by annexing <a href="/wiki/Shilin_District" title="Shilin District">Shilin</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beitou_District" title="Beitou District">Beitou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neihu_District" title="Neihu District">Neihu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nangang_District,_Taipei" title="Nangang District, Taipei">Nangang</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jingmei" title="Jingmei">Jingmei</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Muzha_District" title="Muzha District">Muzha</a>. At that time, the city's total area increased fourfold through absorbing several outlying towns and villages and the population increased to 1.56 million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcghistory_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-tcghistory-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city's population, which had reached one million in the early 1960s, also expanded rapidly after 1967, exceeding two million by the mid-1970s. Although growth within the city itself gradually slowed thereafter<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh199685_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh199685-20">[20]</a></sup> — its population had become relatively stable by the mid-1990s — Taipei remained one of the world's most densely populated urban areas, and the population continued to increase in the region surrounding the city, notably along the corridor between Taipei and <a href="/wiki/Keelung" title="Keelung">Keelung</a>.</p>
<p>In 1990 Taipei's 16 districts were consolidated into the current 12 districts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yearbook_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-yearbook-21">[21]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Wild_Lily_student_movement" title="Wild Lily student movement">Mass democracy rallies</a> that year in the <a href="/wiki/Liberty_Square_(Taipei)" title="Liberty Square (Taipei)">plaza</a> around Chiang Kai-shek Memorial Hall led to an island-wide transition to multi-party <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a>, where legislators are chosen via regularly scheduled popular elections, during the presidency of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lee_Teng-Hui" title="Lee Teng-Hui">Lee Teng-Hui</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TaipeiViewFromMaokong.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3456" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/TaipeiViewFromMaokong.jpg/220px-TaipeiViewFromMaokong.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/TaipeiViewFromMaokong.jpg/330px-TaipeiViewFromMaokong.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/TaipeiViewFromMaokong.jpg/440px-TaipeiViewFromMaokong.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TaipeiViewFromMaokong.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The city of Taipei, as seen from <a href="/wiki/Maokong" title="Maokong">Maokong</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Taipei City is located in the <a href="/wiki/Taipei_Basin" title="Taipei Basin">Taipei Basin</a> in northern <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-taipeiprofile_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-taipeiprofile-22">[22]</a></sup> It is bordered by the <a href="/wiki/Xindian_River" title="Xindian River">Xindian River</a> on the south and the <a href="/wiki/Tamsui_River" title="Tamsui River">Tamsui River</a> on the west. The generally low-lying terrain of the central areas on the western side of the municipality slopes upward to the south and east and especially to the north,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcggeo_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-tcggeo-5">[5]</a></sup> where it reaches 1,120 metres (3,675 ft) at <a href="/wiki/Qixing_Mountain_(Taipei)" title="Qixing Mountain (Taipei)">Qixing Mountain</a>, the highest (inactive) <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcano</a> in Taiwan in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yangmingshan_National_Park" title="Yangmingshan National Park">Yangmingshan National Park</a>. The northern districts of <a href="/wiki/Shilin_District" title="Shilin District">Shilin</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beitou_District" title="Beitou District">Beitou</a> extend north of the <a href="/wiki/Keelung_River" title="Keelung River">Keelung River</a> and are bordered by Yangmingshan National Park. The Taipei city limits cover an area of 271.7997 km<sup>2</sup>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> ranking sixteenth of twenty-five among <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Taiwanese_counties_and_cities_by_area" title="List of Taiwanese counties and cities by area">all counties and cities in Taiwan</a>.</p>
<p>Two peaks, Qixing Mountain and Mt. Datun, rise to the northeast of the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-geopop_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-geopop-24">[24]</a></sup> Qixing Mountain is located on the <a href="/wiki/Tatun_Volcano_Group" title="Tatun Volcano Group">Tatun Volcano Group</a> and the tallest mountain at the rim of the Taipei Basin, with its main peak at 1,120 metres (3,670 ft). Mt. Datun's main peak is 1,092 metres (3,583 ft). These former volcanoes make up the western section of Yangmingshan National Park, extending from Mt. Datun northward to Mt. Caigongkeng (菜公坑山). Located on a broad saddle between two mountains, the area also contains the marshy Datun Pond.</p>
<p>To the southeast of the city lie the Songshan Hills and the Qingshui Ravine, which form a barrier of lush woods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-geopop_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-geopop-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Taipei has a <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">monsoon</a>-influenced <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen</a>: Cfa).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Summers are long-lasting, hot and humid, and accompanied by occasional heavy rainstorms and typhoons, while winters are short, generally warm and generally very <a href="/wiki/Fog" title="Fog">foggy</a> due to the northeasterly winds from the vast <a href="/wiki/Siberian_High" title="Siberian High">Siberian High</a> being intensified by the pooling of this cooler air in the Taipei Basin. As in the rest of Northern Taiwan, daytime temperatures of Taipei can often peak above 26 degrees Celsius during a warm winter day, while they can dip below 26 degrees Celsius during a rainy summer's afternoon. Occasional cold fronts during the winter months can drop the daily temperature by 3 to 5 degrees Celsius, though temperatures rarely drop below 10 degrees Celsius.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Extreme temperatures ranged from −0.2 °C (31.6 °F) on February 13, 1901 to 39.3 °C (102.7 °F) on August 8, 2013, while snow has never been recorded in the city besides on mountains located within the city limit such as <a href="/wiki/Yangmingshan" title="Yangmingshan">Mount Yangmingshan</a>. Due to Taiwan's location in the Pacific Ocean, it is affected by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_typhoon" title="Pacific typhoon">Pacific typhoon</a> season, which occurs between June and October.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_quality">Air quality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Air quality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>When compared to other <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asian</a> cities, Taipei has "excellent" capabilities for managing air quality in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Its rainy climate, location near the coast, and strong environmental regulations have prevented air pollution from becoming a substantial health issue, at least compared to cities in southeast Asia and industrial China. However, smog is extremely common and there is poor visibility throughout the city after rain-less days.</p>
<p>Motor vehicle engine exhaust, particularly from motor scooters, is a source of <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">air pollution</a> in Taipei. There are higher levels of fine <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Particulate" title="Particulate">particulate</a> matter and <a href="/wiki/Polycyclic_aromatic_hydrocarbon" title="Polycyclic aromatic hydrocarbon">polycyclic aromatic hydrocarbons</a> in the mornings because of less air movement; sunlight reduces some pollution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Occasionally, <a href="/wiki/Dust_storm" title="Dust storm">dust storms</a> from <a href="/wiki/Mainland_China" title="Mainland China">Mainland China</a> can temporarily bring extremely poor air quality to the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shilin_night_market_alley.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1186" data-file-width="1934" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Shilin_night_market_alley.jpg/220px-Shilin_night_market_alley.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Shilin_night_market_alley.jpg/330px-Shilin_night_market_alley.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Shilin_night_market_alley.jpg/440px-Shilin_night_market_alley.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

<p>Taipei City is home to 2,704,810 people (2015), while the <a href="/wiki/Taipei%E2%80%93Keelung_metropolitan_area" title="Taipei–Keelung metropolitan area">metropolitan area</a> has a population of 7,047,559 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-population_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-population-6">[6]</a></sup> The population of the city has been decreasing in recent years while the population of the adjacent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Taipei" title="New Taipei">New Taipei</a> has been increasing. The population loss, while rapid in its early years, has been stabilized by new lower density development and campaigns designed to increase birthrate in the city. The population has begun to rise since 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-population_6-3"><a href="#cite_note-population-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-demographics_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-demographics-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Due to Taipei's geography and location in the <a href="/wiki/Taipei_Basin" title="Taipei Basin">Taipei Basin</a> as well as differing times of economic development of its districts, Taipei's population is not evenly distributed. The districts of <a href="/wiki/Da%27an_District,_Taipei" title="Da'an District, Taipei">Daan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Songshan_District,_Taipei" title="Songshan District, Taipei">Songshan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Datong_District,_Taipei" title="Datong District, Taipei">Datong</a> are the most densely populated. These districts, along with adjacent communities such as <a href="/wiki/Yonghe_District" title="Yonghe District">Yonghe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zhonghe_District" title="Zhonghe District">Zhonghe</a> contain some of the most densely populated neighborhoods in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-demographics_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-demographics-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2008, the <a href="/wiki/Birth_rate" title="Birth rate">crude birth rate</a> stood at 7.88% while the <a href="/wiki/Mortality_rate" title="Mortality rate">mortality rate</a> stood at 5.94%. A decreasing and rapidly aging population is an important issue for the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-demographics_34-2"><a href="#cite_note-demographics-34">[34]</a></sup> By the end of 2009, one in ten people in Taipei was over 65 years of age.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Residents who had obtained a college education or higher accounted for 43.48% of the population, and the literacy rate stood at 99.18%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-demographics_34-3"><a href="#cite_note-demographics-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>Like the rest of Taiwan, Taipei is composed of four major ethnic groups: <a href="/wiki/Hoklo_people" title="Hoklo people">Hoklos</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mainlander_(China)" title="Mainlander (China)">Mainlanders</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hakka_people" title="Hakka people">Hakkas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Taiwanese_aborigines" title="Taiwanese aborigines">aborigines</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-demographics_34-4"><a href="#cite_note-demographics-34">[34]</a></sup> Although Hoklos and Mainlanders form the majority of the population of the city, in recent decades many Hakkas have moved into the city. The aboriginal population in the city stands at 12,862 (&lt;0.5%), concentrated mostly in the suburban districts. Foreigners (mainly from <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>) numbered 52,426 at the end of 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-demographics_34-5"><a href="#cite_note-demographics-34">[34]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bellavita_and_CPCCT_head_office_20100907.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Bellavita_and_CPCCT_head_office_20100907.jpg/220px-Bellavita_and_CPCCT_head_office_20100907.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Bellavita_and_CPCCT_head_office_20100907.jpg/330px-Bellavita_and_CPCCT_head_office_20100907.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Bellavita_and_CPCCT_head_office_20100907.jpg/440px-Bellavita_and_CPCCT_head_office_20100907.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bellavita_and_CPCCT_head_office_20100907.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bellavita Shopping Center and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CPC_Corporation,_Taiwan" title="CPC Corporation, Taiwan">CPC</a> Building at Xinyi Business Area</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Neihu_during_2015_winter_solstice.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2422" data-file-width="3229" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Neihu_during_2015_winter_solstice.jpg/220px-Neihu_during_2015_winter_solstice.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Neihu_during_2015_winter_solstice.jpg/330px-Neihu_during_2015_winter_solstice.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Neihu_during_2015_winter_solstice.jpg/440px-Neihu_during_2015_winter_solstice.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Neihu_during_2015_winter_solstice.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Taipei Neihu Technology Park</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Taiwan" title="Economy of Taiwan">Economy of Taiwan</a></div>
<p>As the center of Taiwan's largest conurbation, Taipei has been at the center of rapid economic development in the country and has now become one of the global cities in the production of high technology and its components.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> This is part of the so-called <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_Miracle" title="Taiwan Miracle">Taiwan Miracle</a> which has seen dramatic growth in the city following <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign direct investment</a> in the 1960s. Taiwan is now a <a href="/wiki/Creditor" title="Creditor">creditor</a> economy, holding one of the world's largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_foreign_exchange_reserves" title="List of countries by foreign exchange reserves">foreign exchange reserves</a> of over US$403 billion as of December 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>Despite the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1997_Asian_Financial_Crisis" title="1997 Asian Financial Crisis">Asian financial crisis</a>, the economy continues to expand at about 5% per year, with virtually full employment and low inflation.As of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the nominal GDP per capita in Taipei city is lower than that in Hong Kong by a narrow margin according to The Economist(Nominal GDP per capita in HK is US$38181 in 2013 from IMF).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Furthermore,according to Financial times,GDP per capita based on Purchasing Power Parity(PPP) in Taipei in 2015 is 44173 USD,behind that in Singapore(US$84900 from IMF) and Hong Kong(US$56689 from IMF).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>Taipei and its environs have long been the foremost industrial area of Taiwan, consisting of industries of the <a href="/wiki/Secondary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Secondary sector of the economy">secondary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Tertiary sector of the economy">tertiary</a> sectors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tpctoday_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-tpctoday-41">[41]</a></sup> Most of the country's important factories producing textiles and apparel are located there; other industries include the manufacture of electronic products and components, electrical machinery and equipment, printed materials, precision equipment, and foods and beverages. Such companies include <a href="/wiki/Shihlin_Electric" title="Shihlin Electric">Shihlin Electric</a>, <a href="/wiki/CipherLab" title="CipherLab">CipherLab</a> and <a href="/wiki/Insyde_Software" title="Insyde Software">Insyde Software</a>. Shipbuilding, including yachts and other pleasure craft, is done in the port of <a href="/wiki/Keelung" title="Keelung">Keelung</a> northeast of the city.</p>
<p>Services, including those related to commerce, transportation, and banking, have become increasingly important. Tourism is a small but significant component of the local economy<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> with international visitors totaling almost 3 million in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> Taipei has many top tourist attractions and contributes a significant amount to the US$6.8 billion tourism industry in Taiwan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> National brands such as <a href="/wiki/Asus" title="Asus">ASUS</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chunghwa_Telecom" title="Chunghwa Telecom">Chunghwa Telecom</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_Airlines" title="Mandarin Airlines">Mandarin Airlines</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tatung_Company" title="Tatung Company">Tatung</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Uni_Air" title="Uni Air">Uni Air</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/D-Link" title="D-Link">D-Link</a> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> are headquartered in Taipei City.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chiang_Kai-shek_memorial_amk.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1933" data-file-width="2900" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Chiang_Kai-shek_memorial_amk.jpg/220px-Chiang_Kai-shek_memorial_amk.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Chiang_Kai-shek_memorial_amk.jpg/330px-Chiang_Kai-shek_memorial_amk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Chiang_Kai-shek_memorial_amk.jpg/440px-Chiang_Kai-shek_memorial_amk.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chiang_Kai-shek_memorial_amk.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Chiang_Kai-shek_Memorial_Hall" title="National Chiang Kai-shek Memorial Hall">National Chiang Kai-shek Memorial Hall</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_tourist_attractions_in_Taipei" title="List of tourist attractions in Taipei">List of tourist attractions in Taipei</a></div>
<p>Tourism is a major part of Taipei's economy. In 2013, over 6.3 million overseas visitors visited Taipei, making the city the 15th most visited globally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> The influx of visitors contributed $10.8 billion USD to the city's economy in 2013, the 9th highest in the world and the most of any city in the Chinese-speaking world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Commemorative_sites_and_museums">Commemorative sites and museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Commemorative sites and museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:National_Palace_Museum_Taipei1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/National_Palace_Museum_Taipei1.jpg/220px-National_Palace_Museum_Taipei1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/National_Palace_Museum_Taipei1.jpg/330px-National_Palace_Museum_Taipei1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/National_Palace_Museum_Taipei1.jpg/440px-National_Palace_Museum_Taipei1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:National_Palace_Museum_Taipei1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/National_Palace_Museum" title="National Palace Museum">National Palace Museum</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Chiang_Kai-shek_Memorial_Hall" title="National Chiang Kai-shek Memorial Hall">National Chiang Kai-shek Memorial Hall</a> is a famous monument, landmark and tourist attraction that was erected in memory of General <a href="/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek" title="Chiang Kai-shek">Chiang Kai-shek</a>, former <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Republic_of_China" title="President of the Republic of China">President of the Republic of China</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> The structure stands at the east end of Memorial Hall Square, site of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Concert_Hall_(Taiwan)" title="National Concert Hall (Taiwan)">National Concert Hall</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Theatre_(Taiwan)" title="National Theatre (Taiwan)">National Theater</a> and their adjacent parks as well as the memorial. The landmarks of Liberty Square stand within sight of Taiwan's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Presidential_Building_(Taipei)" title="Presidential Building (Taipei)">Presidential Building</a> in Taipei's <a href="/wiki/Zhongzheng_District" title="Zhongzheng District">Zhongzheng District</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:National_Taiwan_Museum.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/National_Taiwan_Museum.JPG/220px-National_Taiwan_Museum.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/National_Taiwan_Museum.JPG/330px-National_Taiwan_Museum.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/National_Taiwan_Museum.JPG/440px-National_Taiwan_Museum.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:National_Taiwan_Museum.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/National_Taiwan_Museum" title="National Taiwan Museum">National Taiwan Museum</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Taiwan_Museum" title="National Taiwan Museum">National Taiwan Museum</a> sits nearby in what is now <a href="/wiki/228_Peace_Memorial_Park" title="228 Peace Memorial Park">228 Peace Memorial Park</a> and has worn its present name since 1999. The museum is <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>'s oldest, founded on October 24, 1908 by Taiwan's <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_under_Japanese_rule" title="Taiwan under Japanese rule">Japanese colonial government</a> (1895-1945) as the Taiwan Governor's Museum. It was launched with a collection of 10,000 items to celebrate the opening of the island's North-South Railway.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ntminfo_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-ntminfo-56">[56]</a></sup> In 1915 a new museum building opened its doors in what is now <a href="/wiki/228_Peace_Memorial_Park" title="228 Peace Memorial Park">228 Peace Memorial Park</a>. This structure and the adjacent governor's office (now <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Presidential_Building_(Taipei)" title="Presidential Building (Taipei)">Presidential Office Building</a>), served as the two most recognizable public buildings in Taiwan during its period of <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_under_Japanese_rule" title="Taiwan under Japanese rule">Japanese rule</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ntminfo_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-ntminfo-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shung_Ye_Museum_of_Formosan_Aborigines_in_Taipei.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="768" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Shung_Ye_Museum_of_Formosan_Aborigines_in_Taipei.jpg/220px-Shung_Ye_Museum_of_Formosan_Aborigines_in_Taipei.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Shung_Ye_Museum_of_Formosan_Aborigines_in_Taipei.jpg/330px-Shung_Ye_Museum_of_Formosan_Aborigines_in_Taipei.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Shung_Ye_Museum_of_Formosan_Aborigines_in_Taipei.jpg/440px-Shung_Ye_Museum_of_Formosan_Aborigines_in_Taipei.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shung_Ye_Museum_of_Formosan_Aborigines_in_Taipei.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Shung_Ye_Museum_of_Formosan_Aborigines" title="Shung Ye Museum of Formosan Aborigines">Shung Ye Museum of Formosan Aborigines</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Palace_Museum" title="National Palace Museum">National Palace Museum</a> is a vast <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Art_gallery" title="Art gallery">art gallery</a> and <a href="/wiki/Museum" title="Museum">museum</a> built around a permanent collection centered on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_China" title="Ancient China">ancient Chinese artifacts</a>. It should not be confused with the <a href="/wiki/Forbidden_City" title="Forbidden City">Palace Museum</a> in <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a> (which it is named after); both institutions trace their origins to the same institution. The collections were divided in the 1940s as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">Chinese Civil War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-npmwashpo_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-npmwashpo-58">[58]</a></sup> The National Palace Museum in Taipei now boasts a truly international collection while housing one of the world's largest collections of artifacts from ancient China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-npmwashpo_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-npmwashpo-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Shung_Ye_Museum_of_Formosan_Aborigines" title="Shung Ye Museum of Formosan Aborigines">Shung Ye Museum of Formosan Aborigines</a> stands just 200 metres across the road from the National Palace Museum. The museum offers displays of art and historical items by <a href="/wiki/Taiwanese_aborigines" title="Taiwanese aborigines">Taiwanese aborigines</a> along with a range of multimedia displays.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Taipei_Fine_Arts_Museum" title="Taipei Fine Arts Museum">Taipei Fine Arts Museum</a> was established in 1983 as the first museum in Taiwan dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Modern_art" title="Modern art">modern art</a>. The museum is housed in a building designed for the purpose that takes inspiration from Japanese designs. Most art in the collection is by <a href="/wiki/Taiwanese_people" title="Taiwanese people">Taiwanese</a> artists since 1940. Over 3,000 art works are organized into 13 groups.</p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sun_Yat-sen_Memorial_Hall" title="Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall">National Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall</a> near <a href="/wiki/Taipei_101" title="Taipei 101">Taipei 101</a> in <a href="/wiki/Xinyi_District" title="Xinyi District">Xinyi District</a> is named in honor of a founding father of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912%E2%80%9349)" title="Republic of China (1912–49)">Republic of China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sun_Yat-sen" title="Sun Yat-sen">Sun Yat-sen</a>. The hall, completed on May 16, 1972, originally featured exhibits that depicted revolutionary events in <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> at the end of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qing_Dynasty" title="Qing Dynasty">Qing Dynasty</a>. Today it functions as multi-purpose <a href="/wiki/Social_center" title="Social center">social</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Educational" title="Educational">educational</a>, <a href="/wiki/Concert" title="Concert">concert</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cultural" title="Cultural">cultural</a> center for Taiwan's citizens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%E5%8F%B0%E5%8C%97%E7%95%B6%E4%BB%A3%E8%97%9D%E8%A1%93%E9%A4%A8.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/%E5%8F%B0%E5%8C%97%E7%95%B6%E4%BB%A3%E8%97%9D%E8%A1%93%E9%A4%A8.JPG/220px-%E5%8F%B0%E5%8C%97%E7%95%B6%E4%BB%A3%E8%97%9D%E8%A1%93%E9%A4%A8.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/%E5%8F%B0%E5%8C%97%E7%95%B6%E4%BB%A3%E8%97%9D%E8%A1%93%E9%A4%A8.JPG/330px-%E5%8F%B0%E5%8C%97%E7%95%B6%E4%BB%A3%E8%97%9D%E8%A1%93%E9%A4%A8.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/%E5%8F%B0%E5%8C%97%E7%95%B6%E4%BB%A3%E8%97%9D%E8%A1%93%E9%A4%A8.JPG/440px-%E5%8F%B0%E5%8C%97%E7%95%B6%E4%BB%A3%E8%97%9D%E8%A1%93%E9%A4%A8.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%E5%8F%B0%E5%8C%97%E7%95%B6%E4%BB%A3%E8%97%9D%E8%A1%93%E9%A4%A8.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/MoCA_Taipei" title="MoCA Taipei">Museum of Contemporary Art Taipei</a>, aka "old city hall"</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2001 a new museum opened as <a href="/wiki/MoCA_Taipei" title="MoCA Taipei">Museum of Contemporary Art Taipei</a>. The museum is housed in a building that formerly housed Taipei City government offices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tfaminfo_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-tfaminfo-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Taipei_101_at_night.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="989" data-file-width="495" height="440" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Taipei_101_at_night.jpg/220px-Taipei_101_at_night.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Taipei_101_at_night.jpg/330px-Taipei_101_at_night.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Taipei_101_at_night.jpg/440px-Taipei_101_at_night.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Taipei_101_at_night.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Night view of a fully lit <a href="/wiki/Taipei_101" title="Taipei 101">Taipei 101</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Taipei_101">Taipei 101</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Taipei 101">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Taipei_101" title="Taipei 101">Taipei 101</a> is a 101-floor <a href="/wiki/Landmark" title="Landmark">landmark</a> <a href="/wiki/Skyscraper" title="Skyscraper">skyscraper</a> that claimed the title of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World%27s_tallest_structures" title="World's tallest structures">world's tallest building</a> when it opened in 2004, a title it held for six years before relinquishing it to the <a href="/wiki/Burj_Khalifa" title="Burj Khalifa">Burj Khalifa</a> in <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a>. Designed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C.Y._Lee_%26_Partners" title="C.Y. Lee &amp; Partners">C.Y. Lee &amp; Partners</a> and constructed by <a href="/wiki/KTRT_Joint_Venture" title="KTRT Joint Venture">KTRT Joint Venture</a>, Taipei 101 measures 509 m (1,670 ft) from ground to top, making it the first skyscraper in the world to break the half-kilometer mark in height. Built to withstand typhoon winds and earthquake tremors, its design incorporates many engineering innovations and has won numerous international awards. Taipei 101 remains one of the tallest skyscrapers in the world and holds <a href="/wiki/Leadership_in_Energy_and_Environmental_Design" title="Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design">LEED</a>'s certification as the world's largest "green" building. Its shopping mall and its indoor and outdoor observatories draw visitors from all over the world. Taipei 101's <a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Eve" title="New Year's Eve">New Year's Eve</a> fireworks display is a regular feature of international broadcasts.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Performing_arts">Performing arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Performing arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:National_Concert_Hall,_Taipei.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1224" data-file-width="1632" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/National_Concert_Hall%2C_Taipei.jpg/220px-National_Concert_Hall%2C_Taipei.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/National_Concert_Hall%2C_Taipei.jpg/330px-National_Concert_Hall%2C_Taipei.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/National_Concert_Hall%2C_Taipei.jpg/440px-National_Concert_Hall%2C_Taipei.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:National_Concert_Hall,_Taipei.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Taiwan's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Theater_and_Concert_Hall" title="National Theater and Concert Hall">National Concert Hall</a> at night</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Theater_and_Concert_Hall" title="National Theater and Concert Hall">National Theater and Concert Hall</a> stand at Taipei's <a href="/wiki/Liberty_Square_(Taipei)" title="Liberty Square (Taipei)">Liberty Square</a> and host events by foreign and domestic performers. Other leading concert venues include <a href="/wiki/Zhongshan_Hall" title="Zhongshan Hall">Zhongshan Hall</a> at <a href="/wiki/Ximending" title="Ximending">Ximending</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sun_Yat-sen_Memorial_Hall" title="Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall">Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall</a> near <a href="/wiki/Taipei_101" title="Taipei 101">Taipei 101</a>.</p>
<p>A new venue, the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei_Performing_Arts_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Taipei Performing Arts Center (page does not exist)">Taipei Performing Arts Center</a>, is under construction and slated to open in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> The venue will stand near the <a href="/wiki/Shilin_Night_Market" title="Shilin Night Market">Shilin Night Market</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> and will house three theaters for events with multi-week runs. The architectural design, by <a href="/wiki/Rem_Koolhaas" title="Rem Koolhaas">Rem Koolhaas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Office_for_Metropolitan_Architecture" title="Office for Metropolitan Architecture">OMA</a>, was determined in 2009 in an international competition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> The same design process is also in place for a new <a href="/wiki/Taipei_Center_for_Popular_Music" title="Taipei Center for Popular Music">Taipei Center for Popular Music</a> and <a href="/wiki/Taipei_City_Museum" title="Taipei City Museum">Taipei City Museum</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Shopping_and_recreation">Shopping and recreation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Shopping and recreation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Shopping_in_Taipei" title="Shopping in Taipei">Shopping in Taipei</a></div>
<p>Taipei is known for its many <a href="/wiki/Night_markets_in_Taiwan" title="Night markets in Taiwan">night markets</a>, the most famous of which is the <a href="/wiki/Shilin_Night_Market" title="Shilin Night Market">Shilin Night Market</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Shilin_District" title="Shilin District">Shilin District</a>. The surrounding streets by Shilin Night Market are extremely crowded during the evening, usually opening late afternoon and operating well past midnight. Most night markets feature individual stalls selling a mixture of food, clothing, and consumer goods.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ximending_at_night.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1070" data-file-width="969" height="243" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Ximending_at_night.jpg/220px-Ximending_at_night.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Ximending_at_night.jpg/330px-Ximending_at_night.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Ximending_at_night.jpg/440px-Ximending_at_night.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ximending_at_night.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The busy streets of <a href="/wiki/Ximending" title="Ximending">Ximending</a> at night</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ximending" title="Ximending">Ximending</a> has been a famous area for shopping and entertainment since the 1930s. Historic structures include a concert hall, a historic cinema, and the <a href="/wiki/Red_House_Theater" title="Red House Theater">Red House Theater</a>. Modern structures house karaoke businesses, art film cinemas, wide-release movie cinemas, electronic stores, and a wide variety of restaurants and fashion clothing stores.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKelly200799_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKelly200799-66">[66]</a></sup> The pedestrian area is especially popular with teens and has been called the "<a href="/wiki/Harajuku" title="Harajuku">Harajuku</a>" of Taipei.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Taipei_Rushhour_birdseye.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Taipei_Rushhour_birdseye.JPG/220px-Taipei_Rushhour_birdseye.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Taipei_Rushhour_birdseye.JPG/330px-Taipei_Rushhour_birdseye.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Taipei_Rushhour_birdseye.JPG/440px-Taipei_Rushhour_birdseye.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Taipei_Rushhour_birdseye.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Eastern_District_of_Taipei" title="Eastern District of Taipei">Eastern district</a> at night</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The newly developed <a href="/wiki/Xinyi_District" title="Xinyi District">Xinyi District</a> is popular with tourists and locals alike for its many entertainment and shopping venues, as well as being the home of <a href="/wiki/Taipei_101" title="Taipei 101">Taipei 101</a>, a prime tourist attraction. Malls in the area include the sprawling <a href="/wiki/Mitsukoshi" title="Mitsukoshi">Shin Kong Mitsukoshi</a> complex, Breeze Center, Bellavita, Taipei 101 mall, <a href="/wiki/Eslite_Bookstore" title="Eslite Bookstore">Eslite Bookstore</a>'s flagship store (which includes a boutique mall), The Living Mall, ATT shopping mall, and the Vieshow Cinemas (formerly known as Warner Village). The Xinyi district also serves as the center of Taipei's active nightlife, with several popular lounge bars and nightclubs concentrated in a relatively small area around the Neo19, ATT 4 FUN and Taipei 101 buildings. Lounge bars such as Barcode and nightclubs such as Spark and Myst are among the most-visited places here.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Eslite_Bookstore_Xinyi_Store_20091010.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Eslite_Bookstore_Xinyi_Store_20091010.jpg/220px-Eslite_Bookstore_Xinyi_Store_20091010.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Eslite_Bookstore_Xinyi_Store_20091010.jpg/330px-Eslite_Bookstore_Xinyi_Store_20091010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Eslite_Bookstore_Xinyi_Store_20091010.jpg/440px-Eslite_Bookstore_Xinyi_Store_20091010.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Eslite_Bookstore_Xinyi_Store_20091010.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Eslite_Bookstore" title="Eslite Bookstore">Eslite Bookstore</a> in <a href="/wiki/Xinyi_District" title="Xinyi District">Xinyi District</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The thriving shopping area around <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taipei_Main_Station" title="Taipei Main Station">Taipei Main Station</a> includes the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taipei_Underground_Market" title="Taipei Underground Market">Taipei Underground Market</a> and the original Shin Kong <a href="/wiki/Mitsukoshi" title="Mitsukoshi">Mitsukoshi</a> department store at <a href="/wiki/Shin_Kong_Life_Tower" title="Shin Kong Life Tower">Shin Kong Life Tower</a>. Other popular shopping destinations include the <a href="/wiki/Zhongshan_Metro_Mall" title="Zhongshan Metro Mall">Zhongshan Metro Mall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dihua_Street" title="Dihua Street">Dihua Street</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Guang_Hua_Digital_Plaza" title="Guang Hua Digital Plaza">Guang Hua Digital Plaza</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Core_Pacific_City" title="Core Pacific City">Core Pacific City</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Miramar_Entertainment_Park" title="Miramar Entertainment Park">Miramar Entertainment Park</a> is known for its large Ferris wheel and <a href="/wiki/IMAX" title="IMAX">IMAX</a> theater.</p>
<p>Taipei maintains an extensive system of parks, green spaces, and nature preserves. Parks and forestry areas of note in and around the city include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yangmingshan_National_Park" title="Yangmingshan National Park">Yangmingshan National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taipei_Zoo" title="Taipei Zoo">Taipei Zoo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Daan_Forest_Park" title="Daan Forest Park">Da-an Forest Park</a>. <a href="/wiki/Yangmingshan" title="Yangmingshan">Yangmingshan National Park</a> (located 10 kilometres (6.2 mi) north of the central city) is famous for its cherry blossoms, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hot_springs" title="Hot springs">hot springs</a>, and sulfur deposits. It is the home of famous writer <a href="/wiki/Lin_Yutang" title="Lin Yutang">Lin Yutang</a>, the summer residence of <a href="/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek" title="Chiang Kai-shek">Chiang Kai-shek</a>, residences of foreign diplomats, the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Culture_University" title="Chinese Culture University">Chinese Culture University</a>, the meeting place of the now defunct <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_the_Republic_of_China" title="National Assembly of the Republic of China">National Assembly of the Republic of China</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Kuomintang" title="Kuomintang">Kuomintang</a> Party Archives. The <a href="/wiki/Taipei_Zoo" title="Taipei Zoo">Taipei Zoo</a> was founded in 1914 and covers an area of 165 hectares for animal sanctuary.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bitan" title="Bitan">Bitan</a> is known for boating and water sports. <a href="/wiki/Tamsui_District" title="Tamsui District">Tamsui</a> is a popular sea-side resort town. Ocean beaches are accessible in several directions from Taipei.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Temples">Temples</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Temples">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Longshan_Temple_-_Right_entrance.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2207" data-file-width="3022" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Longshan_Temple_-_Right_entrance.jpg/220px-Longshan_Temple_-_Right_entrance.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Longshan_Temple_-_Right_entrance.jpg/330px-Longshan_Temple_-_Right_entrance.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Longshan_Temple_-_Right_entrance.jpg/440px-Longshan_Temple_-_Right_entrance.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Longshan_Temple_-_Right_entrance.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Built in 1738, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mengjia_Longshan_Temple" title="Mengjia Longshan Temple">Longshan Temple</a> is one of the oldest temples in the city.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Street_corner_shrine,_Taipei_2013.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Street_corner_shrine%2C_Taipei_2013.jpg/220px-Street_corner_shrine%2C_Taipei_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Street_corner_shrine%2C_Taipei_2013.jpg/330px-Street_corner_shrine%2C_Taipei_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Street_corner_shrine%2C_Taipei_2013.jpg/440px-Street_corner_shrine%2C_Taipei_2013.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Street_corner_shrine,_Taipei_2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Street corner shrine, Taipei 2013</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Taipei is rich in beautiful, ornate temples housing <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taoism" title="Taoism">Taoist</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_folk_religion" title="Chinese folk religion">Chinese folk religion</a> deities. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mengjia_Longshan_Temple" title="Mengjia Longshan Temple">Longshan Temple</a>, built in 1738 and located in the <a href="/wiki/Wanhua_District" title="Wanhua District">Wanhua District</a>, demonstrates an example of architecture with southern <a href="/wiki/Chinese_architecture" title="Chinese architecture">Chinese influences</a> commonly seen on older buildings in Taiwan.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Xinsheng_Road" title="Xinsheng Road">Xinsheng South Road</a> is known as the "Road to Heaven" due to its high concentration of temples, shrines, churches, and mosques.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Other famous temples include <a href="/wiki/Dalongdong_Baoan_Temple" title="Dalongdong Baoan Temple">Baoan Temple</a> located in historic <a href="/wiki/Dalongdong" title="Dalongdong">Dalongdong</a>, a national historical site, and Xiahai City God Temple, located in the old Dadaocheng community, constructed with architecture similar to temples in southern <a href="/wiki/Fujian" title="Fujian">Fujian</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-temples_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-temples-70">[70]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Taipei_Confucius_Temple" title="Taipei Confucius Temple">Taipei Confucius Temple</a> traces its history back to 1879 during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qing_Dynasty" title="Qing Dynasty">Qing Dynasty</a> and also incorporates southern Fujian-style architecture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>Besides large temples, small outdoor shrines to local deities are very common and can be spotted on road sides, parks, and neighborhoods. Many homes and businesses may also set up small shrines of candles, figurines, and offerings. Some restaurants, for example, may set up a small shrine to the Kitchen god for success in a restaurant business.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Taipei_101_2008_NewYear_Firework.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="867" height="304" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Taipei_101_2008_NewYear_Firework.jpg/220px-Taipei_101_2008_NewYear_Firework.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Taipei_101_2008_NewYear_Firework.jpg/330px-Taipei_101_2008_NewYear_Firework.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Taipei_101_2008_NewYear_Firework.jpg/440px-Taipei_101_2008_NewYear_Firework.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Taipei_101_2008_NewYear_Firework.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Eve" title="New Year's Eve">New Year's Eve</a> fireworks at <a href="/wiki/Taipei_101" title="Taipei 101">Taipei 101</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
