<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals_and_events">Festivals and events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Festivals and events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Many yearly festivals are held in Taipei. In recent years some festivals, such as the Double Ten Day fireworks and concerts, are increasingly hosted on a rotating basis by a number of cities around Taiwan.</p>
<p>When <a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Eve" title="New Year's Eve">New Year's Eve</a> arrives on the <a href="/wiki/Solar_calendar" title="Solar calendar">solar calendar</a>, thousands of people converge on Taipei's <a href="/wiki/Xinyi_District" title="Xinyi District">Xinyi District</a> for <a href="/wiki/Parade" title="Parade">parades</a>, outdoor <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Concerts" title="Concerts">concerts</a> by <a href="/wiki/Mandopop" title="Mandopop">popular artists</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Street_performer" title="Street performer">street shows</a>, round-the clock <a href="/wiki/Nightlife" title="Nightlife">nightlife</a>. The high point is of course the countdown to midnight, when <a href="/wiki/Taipei_101" title="Taipei 101">Taipei 101</a> assumes the role of the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Fireworks" title="Fireworks">fireworks</a> platform.</p>
<p>The Taipei <a href="/wiki/Lantern_Festival" title="Lantern Festival">Lantern Festival</a> concludes the <a href="/wiki/Lunar_New_Year" title="Lunar New Year">Lunar New Year</a> holiday. The timing of the city's lantern exhibit coincides with the national festival in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pingxi,_Taipei" title="Pingxi, Taipei">Pingxi</a>, when thousands of fire lanterns are released into the sky.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tourism_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-tourism-73">[73]</a></sup> The city's lantern exhibit rotates among different downtown locales from year to year, including <a href="/wiki/Liberty_Square_(Taipei)" title="Liberty Square (Taipei)">Liberty Square</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taipei_101" title="Taipei 101">Taipei 101</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Zhongshan_Hall" title="Zhongshan Hall">Zhongshan Hall</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ximending" title="Ximending">Ximending</a>.</p>
<p>On <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Double_Ten_Day" title="Double Ten Day">Double Ten Day</a>, patriotic celebrations are held in front of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Presidential_Office_Building,_Taipei" title="Presidential Office Building, Taipei">Presidential Building</a>. Other annual festivals include <a href="/wiki/Qingming_Festival" title="Qingming Festival">Ancestors Day (Tomb-Sweeping Day)</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Duanwu_Festival" title="Duanwu Festival">Dragon Boat Festival</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ghost_Festival" title="Ghost Festival">Ghost Festival</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Mid-Autumn_Festival" title="Mid-Autumn Festival">Mid-Autumn Festival (Moon Festival)</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tourism_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-tourism-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>Taipei regularly hosts its share of international events. The city recently hosted the 2009 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Summer_Deaflympics" title="Summer Deaflympics">Summer Deaflympics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> This event was followed by the <a href="/wiki/Taipei_International_Flora_Exposition" title="Taipei International Flora Exposition">Taipei International Flora Exposition</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Garden_festival" title="Garden festival">garden festival</a> hosted from November 2010 to April 2011. The Floral Expo was the first of its kind to take place in Taiwan and only the seventh hosted in <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>; the expo admitted 110,000 visitors on February 27, 2011.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Romanization">Romanization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Romanization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language_romanization_in_Taiwan" title="Chinese language romanization in Taiwan">Chinese language romanization in Taiwan</a></div>
<p>The spelling "Taipei" derives from the <a href="/wiki/Wade%E2%80%93Giles" title="Wade–Giles">Wade–Giles</a> romanization <i>T'ai-pei.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> The name could be also romanized as <i>Táiběi</i> according to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hanyu_Pinyin" title="Hanyu Pinyin">Hanyu Pinyin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tongyong_Pinyin" title="Tongyong Pinyin">Tongyong Pinyin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pinyin_tt_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-pinyin_tt-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pinyin_cp_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-pinyin_cp-77">[77]</a></sup></p>

</div>
<p>Taipei City is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_municipality_of_Taiwan" title="Special municipality of Taiwan">special municipality</a> which is directly under the <a href="/wiki/Executive_Yuan" title="Executive Yuan">Executive Yuan</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Government" title="Central Government">Central Government</a>) of <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">ROC</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Taipei" title="Mayor of Taipei">mayor of Taipei City</a> had been an appointed position since Taipei's conversion to a centrally administered municipality in 1967 until the first public election was held in 1994.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> The position has a four-year term and is elected by direct popular vote. The first elected mayor was <a href="/wiki/Chen_Shui-bian" title="Chen Shui-bian">Chen Shui-bian</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Progressive_Party" title="Democratic Progressive Party">Democratic Progressive Party</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ma_Ying-jeou" title="Ma Ying-jeou">Ma Ying-jeou</a> took office in 1998 for two terms, before handing it over to <a href="/wiki/Hau_Lung-pin" title="Hau Lung-pin">Hau Lung-pin</a> who won the 2006 mayoral election on December 9, 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> Both Chen Shui-bian and Ma Ying-Jeou went on to become <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Republic_of_China" title="President of the Republic of China">President of the Republic of China</a>. The incumbent mayor, <a href="/wiki/Ko_Wen-je" title="Ko Wen-je">Ko Wen-je</a>, was elected on November 29, 2014 and took office on December 25, 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>Based on the outcomes of previous elections in the past decade, the vote of the overall constituency of Taipei City shows a slight inclination towards the pro-KMT camp (the <a href="/wiki/Pan-Blue_Coalition" title="Pan-Blue Coalition">Pan-Blue Coalition</a>);<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> however, the pro-DPP camp (the <a href="/wiki/Pan-Green_Coalition" title="Pan-Green Coalition">Pan-Green Coalition</a>) also has considerable support.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ketagalan_Boulevard" title="Ketagalan Boulevard">Ketagalan Boulevard</a>, where the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Presidential_Office_Building,_Taipei" title="Presidential Office Building, Taipei">Presidential Office Building</a> and other government structures are situated, is often the site of mass gatherings such as inauguration and national holiday parades, receptions for visiting dignitaries, political demonstrations,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> and public festivals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Garbage_recycling">Garbage recycling</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Garbage recycling">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Taipei City is also famous for its effort in garbage recycling, which has become such a good international precedent that other countries have sent teams to study the recycling system. After the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environmental_Protection_Administration_(Republic_of_China)" title="Environmental Protection Administration (Republic of China)">Environmental Protection Administration</a> (EPA) established a program in 1998 combining the efforts of communities, a financial resource named the Recycling Fund was made available to recycling companies and waste collectors. Manufacturers, vendors and importers of recyclable waste pay fees to the Fund, which uses the money to set firm prices for recyclables and subsidize local recycling efforts. Between 1998 and 2008, the recycling rate increased from 6 percent to 32 percent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> This improvement enabled the government of Taipei to demonstrate its recycling system to the world at the <a href="/wiki/Expo_2010" title="Expo 2010">Shanghai World Expo 2010</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Taipei City is divided up into 12 administrative <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/District_(ROC)" title="District (ROC)">districts</a> (區 <i>qu</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> Each district is further divided up into <a href="/wiki/Village_(Taiwan)" title="Village (Taiwan)">urban villages</a> (里), which are further sub-divided up into neighborhoods (鄰).</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="City_planning">City planning</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: City planning">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city is characterized by straight roads and public buildings of grand Western architectural styles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jones_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-jones-88">[88]</a></sup> The city is built on a square grid configuration, however these blocks are huge by international standards with 500 m (1,640.42 ft) sides. The area in between these blocks are infilled with lanes and alleys, which provide access to quieter residential or mixed-use development. Other than a citywide 30 kilometres per hour (19 mph) speed limit, there is little uniform planning within this "hidden" area; therefore lanes (perpendicular to streets) and alleys (parallel with street, or conceptually, perpendicular to the lane) spill out from the main throughways. These minor roads are not always perpendicular and sometimes cut through the block diagonally.</p>
<p>Although development began in the western districts (still considered the cultural heart of the city) of the city due to trade, the eastern districts of the city have become the focus of recent development projects. Many of the western districts, already in decline, have become targets of new <a href="/wiki/Urban_renewal" title="Urban renewal">urban renewal</a> initiatives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jones_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-jones-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wende_Station_platform.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Wende_Station_platform.jpg/220px-Wende_Station_platform.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Wende_Station_platform.jpg/330px-Wende_Station_platform.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Wende_Station_platform.jpg/440px-Wende_Station_platform.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wende_Station_platform.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Platform of <a href="/wiki/Wende_Station" title="Wende Station">Wende Station</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Taipei_Metro" title="Taipei Metro">Taipei Metro</a> system.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Public_transport" title="Public transport">Public transport</a> accounts for a substantial portion of different modes of transport in Taiwan, with Taipei residents having the highest utilization rate at 34.1%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pubtrans_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-pubtrans-89">[89]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Private_transport" title="Private transport">Private transport</a> consists of <a href="/wiki/Scooter_(motorcycle)" title="Scooter (motorcycle)">motor scooters</a>, private cars, and <a href="/wiki/Bicycle" title="Bicycle">bicycles</a>. Motor-scooters often weave between cars and occasionally through oncoming traffic. Respect for traffic laws, once scant, has improved with deployment of traffic cameras and increasing numbers of police roadblocks checking riders for alcohol consumption and other offenses.</p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taipei_Station" title="Taipei Station">Taipei Station</a> serves as the comprehensive hub for the subway, bus, conventional rail, and high-speed rail.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tpctoday_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-tpctoday-41">[41]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Contactless_smart_card" title="Contactless smart card">contactless smartcard</a>, known as <a href="/wiki/EasyCard" title="EasyCard">EasyCard</a>, can be used for all modes of public transit as well as several retail outlets. It contains credits that are deducted each time a ride is taken.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> The EasyCard is read via <a href="/wiki/Proximity_sensor" title="Proximity sensor">proximity sensory panels</a> on buses and in MRT stations, and it does not need to be removed from one's wallet or purse.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Metro">Metro</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Metro">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Taipei_Metro" title="Taipei Metro">Taipei Metro</a></div>
<p>Taipei's public transport system, the <a href="/wiki/Taipei_Metro" title="Taipei Metro">Taipei Metro</a> (commonly referred to as the MRT), incorporates a <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">metro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">light rail</a> system based on advanced <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A9hicule_Automatique_L%C3%A9ger" title="Véhicule Automatique Léger">VAL</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Transportation" title="Bombardier Transportation">Bombardier</a> technology. There are currently five metro lines that are labelled in three ways: color, line number and depot station name. In addition to the rapid transit system itself, the Taipei Metro also includes several public facilities such as the <a href="/wiki/Maokong_Gondola" title="Maokong Gondola">Maokong Gondola</a>, underground shopping malls, parks, and public squares. Modifications to existing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taiwan_Railway_Administration" title="Taiwan Railway Administration">railway</a> lines to integrate them into the metro system are underway, as well as a rapid transit line to connect the city with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taiwan_Taoyuan_International_Airport" title="Taiwan Taoyuan International Airport">Taiwan Taoyuan International Airport</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taoyuan_City" title="Taoyuan City">Taoyuan City</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Taipei_Railway_Station_Front.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Taipei_Railway_Station_Front.jpg/220px-Taipei_Railway_Station_Front.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Taipei_Railway_Station_Front.jpg/330px-Taipei_Railway_Station_Front.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Taipei_Railway_Station_Front.jpg/440px-Taipei_Railway_Station_Front.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Taipei_Railway_Station_Front.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Taipei Railway Station front</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_High_Speed_Rail" title="Taiwan High Speed Rail">Taiwan High Speed Rail</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taiwan_Railway_Administration" title="Taiwan Railway Administration">Taiwan Railway Administration</a></div>
<p>Beginning in 1983, surface rail lines in the city were moved underground as part of the <a href="/wiki/Taipei_Railway_Underground_Project" title="Taipei Railway Underground Project">Taipei Railway Underground Project</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_High_Speed_Rail" title="Taiwan High Speed Rail">Taiwan High Speed Rail</a> system opened in 2007. The bullet trains connect Taipei with the west coast cities of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Taipei" title="New Taipei">New Taipei</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taoyuan_City" title="Taoyuan City">Taoyuan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hsinchu" title="Hsinchu">Hsinchu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taichung" title="Taichung">Taichung</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chiayi" title="Chiayi">Chiayi</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tainan_City" title="Tainan City">Tainan</a> before terminating at <a href="/wiki/Zuoying_District" title="Zuoying District">Zuoying</a> (<a href="/wiki/Kaohsiung" title="Kaohsiung">Kaohsiung</a>) at speeds that cut travel times by 60% or more from what they normally are on a bus or conventional train.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taiwan_Railway_Administration" title="Taiwan Railway Administration">Taiwan Railway Administration</a> also runs passenger and freight services throughout the entire island.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus">Bus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Bus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Taipei_Joint_Bus_System" title="Taipei Joint Bus System">Taipei Joint Bus System</a></div>
<p>An extensive <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taipei_bus" title="Taipei bus">city bus system</a> serves metropolitan areas not covered by the metro, with exclusive bus lanes to facilitate transportation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tpctoday_41-2"><a href="#cite_note-tpctoday-41">[41]</a></sup> Riders of the city metro system are able to use the EasyCard for discounted fares on buses, and vice versa. Several major intercity bus terminals are located throughout the city, including the <a href="/wiki/Taipei_Bus_Station" title="Taipei Bus Station">Taipei Bus Station</a> and <a href="/wiki/Taipei_City_Hall_Bus_Station" title="Taipei City Hall Bus Station">Taipei City Hall Bus Station</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Taipei_Songshan_Airport_1st_Terminal_Building_20090926.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Taipei_Songshan_Airport_1st_Terminal_Building_20090926.JPG/220px-Taipei_Songshan_Airport_1st_Terminal_Building_20090926.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Taipei_Songshan_Airport_1st_Terminal_Building_20090926.JPG/330px-Taipei_Songshan_Airport_1st_Terminal_Building_20090926.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Taipei_Songshan_Airport_1st_Terminal_Building_20090926.JPG/440px-Taipei_Songshan_Airport_1st_Terminal_Building_20090926.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Taipei_Songshan_Airport_1st_Terminal_Building_20090926.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Taipei Songshan Airport</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">Airports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Airports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taiwan_Taoyuan_International_Airport" title="Taiwan Taoyuan International Airport">Taiwan Taoyuan International Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Taipei_Songshan_Airport" title="Taipei Songshan Airport">Taipei Songshan Airport</a></div>
<p>Most scheduled international flights are served by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taiwan_Taoyuan_International_Airport" title="Taiwan Taoyuan International Airport">Taiwan Taoyuan International Airport</a> in nearby <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taoyuan_City" title="Taoyuan City">Taoyuan City</a>. <a href="/wiki/Taipei_Songshan_Airport" title="Taipei Songshan Airport">Songshan Airport</a> at the heart of the city in the <a href="/wiki/Songshan_District,_Taipei" title="Songshan District, Taipei">Songshan District</a> serves domestic flights and scheduled flights to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tokyo_International_Airport" title="Tokyo International Airport">Tokyo International Airport</a> (also known as <a href="/wiki/Haneda_Airport" title="Haneda Airport">Haneda Airport</a>), <a href="/wiki/Gimpo_International_Airport" title="Gimpo International Airport">Gimpo International Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Seoul" title="Seoul">Seoul</a>, and about 15 destinations in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People's Republic of China">People's Republic of China</a>. Songshan Airport is accessible by the Taipei Metro <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neihu_Line_(TRTS)" title="Neihu Line (TRTS)">Neihu Line</a>; Taiwan Taoyuan International Airport is not yet accessible by rail, but a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taoyuan_International_Airport_Access_MRT_System" title="Taoyuan International Airport Access MRT System">line</a> is under construction.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ticketing">Ticketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Ticketing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1994, with the rapid development of Taipei, a white paper for transport policies expressed the strong objective to "create a civilised transport system for the people of Taipei." In 1999, they chose Mitac consortium, which Thales-Transportation Systems is part of. <a href="/wiki/Thales_Group" title="Thales Group">Thales</a> was then selected again in 2005 to deploy an upgrade of Taipei's public transport network with an end-to-end and fully contactless automatic fare collection solution that integrates 116 metro stations, 5,000 buses and 92 car parks.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p><a href="/wiki/National_Taiwan_University" title="National Taiwan University">National Taiwan University</a> (NTU) was established in 1928 during the period of Japanese colonial rule. NTU has produced many political and social leaders in Taiwan. Both <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pan-blue_coalition" title="Pan-blue coalition">pan-blue</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pan-green_coalition" title="Pan-green coalition">pan-green</a> movements in Taiwan are rooted on the NTU campus. The university has six campuses in the greater Taipei region (including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Taipei" title="New Taipei">New Taipei</a>) and two additional campuses in <a href="/wiki/Nantou_County" title="Nantou County">Nantou County</a>. The university governs farms, forests, and hospitals for educational and research purposes. The main campus is in Taipei's Da-An district, where most department buildings and all the administrative buildings are located. The College of Law and the College of Medicine are located near the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Presidential_Building_(Taiwan)" title="Presidential Building (Taiwan)">Presidential Building</a>. The <a href="/wiki/National_Taiwan_University_Hospital" title="National Taiwan University Hospital">National Taiwan University Hospital</a> is a leading international center of medical research.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/National_Taiwan_Normal_University" title="National Taiwan Normal University">National Taiwan Normal University</a> (NTNU or <i>Shida</i>) likewise traces its origins to the Japanese colonial period. Originally a teacher training institution, NTNU has developed into a comprehensive international university with demanding entrance requirements. The university boasts especially strong programs in the humanities and international education. Worldwide it is perhaps best known as home of the <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_Training_Center" title="Mandarin Training Center">Mandarin Training Center</a>, a program that offers Mandarin language training each year to over a thousand students from dozens of countries throughout the world. The main campus in Taipei's Da-An district, near MRT Guting Station, is known for its historic architecture and giving its name to the Shida Night Market, one of the most popular among the numerous night markets in Taipei.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Taipei_Arena_20090330.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Taipei_Arena_20090330.jpg/220px-Taipei_Arena_20090330.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Taipei_Arena_20090330.jpg/330px-Taipei_Arena_20090330.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Taipei_Arena_20090330.jpg/440px-Taipei_Arena_20090330.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

<a href="/wiki/Tianmu_Baseball_Stadium" title="Tianmu Baseball Stadium">Tianmu Baseball Stadium</a></div>

<p>Due to Taiwan being under American and Japanese influence over the years, the sports of <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">baseball</a> in particular and <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> have become popular in the city. Taipei, like the rest of the country, has featured most prominently in baseball and has often been the venue for the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Baseball_Championship" title="Asian Baseball Championship">Asian Baseball Championship</a> since the 1960s.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_sporting_events">Major sporting events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Major sporting events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Below is a list of recent sporting events hosted by the city:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/2001_Asian_Baseball_Championship" title="2001 Asian Baseball Championship">2001 Asian Baseball Championship</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/2001_Baseball_World_Cup" title="2001 Baseball World Cup">2001 Baseball World Cup</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/2001_AFC_Women%27s_Championship" title="2001 AFC Women's Championship">2001 AFC Women's Championship</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/2004_FIFA_Futsal_World_Championship" title="2004 FIFA Futsal World Championship">2004 FIFA Futsal World Championship</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/2007_Baseball_World_Cup" title="2007 Baseball World Cup">2007 Baseball World Cup</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/2009_Summer_Deaflympics" title="2009 Summer Deaflympics">2009 Summer Deaflympics</a></li>
</ul>
<p>Taipei will also host the <a href="/wiki/2017_Summer_Universiade" title="2017 Summer Universiade">2017 Summer Universiade</a></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Taipei_Arena" title="Taipei Arena">Taipei Arena</a> is located at the site of the former <a href="/wiki/Taipei_Municipal_Baseball_Stadium" title="Taipei Municipal Baseball Stadium">Taipei Municipal Baseball Stadium</a> (demolished in 2000), with a capacity of over 15,000. Designed by Archasia, the arena was opened on December 1, 2005. Since its opening in 2005, the arena has held more art and cultural activities (such as live concerts) than sporting events, which it was originally designed and built for. The main arena has an adjustable floor space: its minimum floor space is 60 m × 30 m (196.85 <a href="/wiki/Foot_(unit)" title="Foot (unit)">ft</a> × 98.43 ft), and can be extended to 80 m × 40 m (262.47 <a href="/wiki/Foot_(unit)" title="Foot (unit)">ft</a> × 131.23 ft). The <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Taipei" title="Chinese Taipei">Chinese Taipei</a> Ice Hockey League (CIHL) plays out of the auxiliary arena, which is a 60 m × 30 m (196.85 <a href="/wiki/Foot_(unit)" title="Foot (unit)">ft</a> × 98.43 ft) ice skating rink.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Tianmu_Baseball_Stadium" title="Tianmu Baseball Stadium">Tianmu Baseball Stadium</a> is the major baseball venue in Taipei.</p>
<p>Taipei has the only <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_(soccer)" title="Football (soccer)">football</a>-<a href="/wiki/Soccer-specific_stadium" title="Soccer-specific stadium">specific stadium</a> in Taiwan, <a href="/wiki/Zhongshan_Soccer_Stadium" title="Zhongshan Soccer Stadium">Zhongshan Soccer Stadium</a>, which hosts the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Taipei_national_football_team" title="Chinese Taipei national football team">national football team</a>. It hosts qualifiers for the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World</a> and <a href="/wiki/Asian_Football_Confederation" title="Asian Football Confederation">AFC</a> regional cups, and finals of school football tournaments. Since there are no professional football leagues in Taiwan, no other sporting events are held there, since 2009, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taipei_Stadium" title="Taipei Stadium">Taipei Stadium</a> hosts the Soccer and Athletic events.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Youth_baseball">Youth baseball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Youth baseball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2010, a Taipei baseball team — Chung-Ching Junior Little League — won the <a href="/wiki/Junior_League_World_Series#List_of_champions" title="Junior League World Series">Junior League World Series</a>, after winning the Asia-Pacific Region, then defeating the Mexico Region and Latin America Region champions to become the International champion, and finally defeating the U.S. champion (Southwest Region), Rose Capital East LL (Tyler, Texas), 9-1.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. Its <a href="/wiki/Little_League_World_Series" title="Little League World Series">Little League World Series</a> international team has won 17 championships, the most wins in the league.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Taiwan_TVBS_Nangang_Building.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Taiwan_TVBS_Nangang_Building.JPG/220px-Taiwan_TVBS_Nangang_Building.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Taiwan_TVBS_Nangang_Building.JPG/330px-Taiwan_TVBS_Nangang_Building.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Taiwan_TVBS_Nangang_Building.JPG/440px-Taiwan_TVBS_Nangang_Building.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>

TVBS-G produces programs mainly from their <a href="/wiki/Nangang_District,_Taipei" title="Nangang District, Taipei">Nangang</a> building in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taipei_City" title="Taipei City">Taipei City</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As the capital, Taipei City is the headquarters for many television and radio stations in Taiwan and the center of some of the country's largest newspapers.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Newspapers">Newspapers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Newspapers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Newspapers include <i><a href="/wiki/Apple_Daily_(Taiwan)" title="Apple Daily (Taiwan)">Apple Daily</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Central_Daily_News" title="Central Daily News">Central Daily News</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_China_Post" title="The China Post">The China Post</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/China_Times" title="China Times">China Times</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Kinmen_Daily_News" title="Kinmen Daily News">Kinmen Daily News</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Liberty_Times" title="Liberty Times">Liberty Times</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Mandarin_Daily_News" title="Mandarin Daily News">Mandarin Daily News</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Matsu_Daily" title="Matsu Daily">Matsu Daily</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Min_Sheng_Bao" title="Min Sheng Bao">Min Sheng Bao</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Sharp_Daily" title="Sharp Daily">Sharp Daily</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Taipei_Times" title="Taipei Times">Taipei Times</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Taiwan_Daily" title="Taiwan Daily">Taiwan Daily</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Taiwan_News" title="Taiwan News">Taiwan News</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Taiwan_Times" title="Taiwan Times">Taiwan Times</a></i>and <i><a href="/wiki/United_Daily_News" title="United Daily News">United Daily News</a></i>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Taipei is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Network_of_Major_Cities_21" title="Asian Network of Major Cities 21">Asian Network of Major Cities 21</a>.</p>

<td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="2" style="padding:0.5em 0 0.3em; line-height:1.3em;">
<div><b>*</b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transcontinental_country" title="Transcontinental country">Transcontinental country</a>.<br/>
<b>†</b> See: <a href="/wiki/Positions_on_Jerusalem" title="Positions on Jerusalem">Positions on Jerusalem</a>. Both Israel and Palestinians claim Jerusalem as capital. <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a> contains the Israeli parliament and almost all Israeli government ministries. <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">Tel Aviv</a> contains most foreign embassies in Israel; <a href="/wiki/Ramallah" title="Ramallah">Ramallah</a> is the administrative seat of the Palestinian Authority.<br/>
<b>+</b> According to the 1947 <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Republic_of_China" title="Constitution of the Republic of China">Constitution of the Republic of China</a>, Nanjing is the official capital of the ROC, with Taipei as the <a href="/wiki/Temporary_capital" title="Temporary capital">seat of government</a>. See also <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_Taiwan" title="Political status of Taiwan">Political status of Taiwan</a>.</div>

<td class="navbox-list navbox-odd" colspan="2" style="width:100%;padding:0px;background:transparent;color:inherit;">
<div style="padding:0px;">
<table class="navbox-columns-table" style="border-spacing: 0px; text-align:left;width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">
<tr style="vertical-align:top;">
<td style="padding:0px;padding-left:0.25em;;;;width:20%;">
<div>
